⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على الكعبي القائل: إن النعمة تنتقص بالمنة: فاعترض الكعبي على هذا، وزعم أن إعطاء ذلك بطريق الثواب أنفع للصبي من إعطائه ابتداء بالتفضل لما في الإعطاء ابتداء من لحوق المنة وفي الوصول بطريق العوض من ارتفاعها، لما لا منة فما ينال بطريق الأعواض، والمنة تنقص النعمة فيكون ما نيل بطريق العوض أهنأ وألذ. وله قيل: هذا كلام من عرف الله تعالى لا يستجيز من نفسه أن يخطر بباله فضلاً عن التكلم والاحتجاج بمثله عند ملاقاة الخصوم، وذلك لأن النعم كلها من الله تعالى وله علينا المنة العظمى ونتلذذ بالنعم بامتنانه ومن كانت منته عليه أوفر كان هو بذلك أسر وقلبه أفرح وعيشه ألذ، فلو كانت منته تهدم الصنيعة وتنقص النعمة ينبغي أن تكون نعمة الهداية منغصة مكدرة على المؤمنين حيث قال تعالى: ﴿ بَلِ الله يمنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ أَنْ هَدَنكُمْ لِلإِيمَنِ ﴾ ثم لو عرف في هذا التائه في دينه المتحير في أمره علة تنغص النعم بالمن في الشاهد لما تكلم بهذا الكلام الشنيع مسمعه الفظيع موقعه، وذلك أن علة تنغص النعمة في الشاهد بلحوق المنة استواء المنعم والمنعم عليه في الجوهر وتفاوتهما في الحال والرتبة، ثم فوز أحدهما بالسعة في المال والرفعة والجلال في الشاهد والحال وحرمان الآخر عن كل ذلك، ثم إن الفائز بالنعم المختص بمزية في السعة والميسرة والجاه والمقدرة اتخذ يدًا بمكان صاحبه وأدر عليه سوابغ نعمه، فيرى المنعم عليه نفسه تحت منته ورهن مباره وأياديه ورقبته كالمسترقة له مع أن تبدل الحال مترتب تحت الإمكان الأقرب والتصور الأيسر فتتنغص عليه النعمة بمقابلة ما يرى برقبته مسترقة لمن يساويه في الرتبة أو يقاربه في الدرجة والمنزلة حتى إن تبدل الحال لو كان من الممكنات الأبعدية والموهومات القصية بأن اختص ملك من الملوك في الأرض أو عظيم من عظماء المملكة بعض السوقة واحد من أمناء الناس وجعله أهلاً لأحبته ومباره واتخذه غيبة لأسراره أو ساق عليه السلطان الأعظم إلى حد من أكابر أبناء دولته وأشياع دعوته أموالاً خطيرة، وخلع عليه خلعًا نفيسة لعد المنعم عليه ذلك من أجل مفاخره وأعظم مآثره ومهما ازداد حظه من ذلك ازداد في نفسه ارتياحا وفي قلبه انفساحًا وانشراحا، ويمثله لو أن أحد من هؤلاء الأكابر والعظماء اشترى شيئًا من أحد وأوفاه ثمنه لم يحصل للبائع بذلك سبب فخر ولا يثبت له عند الناس منزلة وقدر، وكان ما نيل من السلطان بالامتنان والإنعام ألذ وأشهى وأهنأ عند كل العقلاء، وأمرًا هذا مع كون تقلب الحال وتبدل الشأن مترتبا تحت الإمكان وإن بعد وداخلاً في حيز التصور وإن تعذر في العادات ونذر، فكيف يتوهم أن تتنغص نعمه وإن صغرت في ذاتها وقلت في نفسها بلحوق منة من قبل الجبار المتكبر القهار المقتدر الذي كل شيء وإن عظم قدره وجل خطره داخل في ملكوته وخاضع لجبروته، يعز من يعز بإحسانه وإفضاله ويذل من يذل بإهانته وإذلاله، لا زوال لملكه وسلطانه ولا تبدل لتذلل العبد وادعائه بل التبدل والزوال يدخلان في حيز
Refutation of al-Ka'bi who says: 'Blessings are diminished by obligation.' So al-Ka'bi objected to this [previous assertion] and claimed that giving that [compensation] by way of reward is more beneficial for the boy than giving it initially by way of grace/voluntary favor, because giving initially entails the attachment of obligation, while obtaining by way of compensation involves its removal, since there is no obligation in what is obtained by way of compensations, and obligation diminishes the blessing; thus what is obtained by way of compensation is more wholesome and delightful. And it was said to him: This is the speech of one who does not know Allah Most High—he would not permit himself to let such a thought cross his mind, let alone speak and argue with it when facing opponents. This is because all blessings are from Allah Most High, and He has the supreme obligation over us, and we delight in blessings through His bestowal of obligation; and one upon whom His obligation is more abundant is thereby more joyous, his heart more happy, and his life more delightful. If His obligation destroyed the favor and diminished the blessing, then the blessing of guidance would necessarily be spoiled and troubled for the believers, since He said: 'But Allah confers obligation upon you that He has guided you to faith.' Moreover, if this confused person in his religion, bewildered in his affair, knew the cause that spoils blessings by obligation in the witnessed world, he would not utter this ugly speech with its terrible sound and [bad] position. For the cause of the spoiling of blessing in the witnessed world by the attachment of obligation is the equality of the benefactor and the benefited in essence, and their difference in state and rank; then the one who wins by abundance in wealth, elevation, and majesty in the witnessed world and state, and the deprivation of the other from all that; then the one who is granted blessings, distinguished by a privilege in abundance, ease, status, and capability, [takes it as] a hand over his companion and causes his abundant blessings to flow upon him. So the one benefited sees himself under his obligation, bound to his favors, benefactions, and acts of kindness, as if he is subservient to him, while the change of state is subject to the nearest possibility and easiest conception, so the blessing becomes spoiled for him in comparison to what he sees as subservient to his neck for one who is equal to him in rank or close to him in degree and station. Until if the change of state were among the most distant possibilities and far-fetched imaginations—such as a king among the kings of the earth or a great one among the greats of the kingdom especially [favors] some commoner, one of the trusted people, and makes him worthy of his beloved ones and favors, and takes him as a confidant for his secrets, or the supreme ruler conveys to him from the greatest of the sons of his state and supporters of his cause enormous wealth, and bestows upon him precious robes of honor—the one benefited would count that among his greatest honors and most magnificent achievements; and the more his fortune increases from that, the more he increases in joy in himself and expansion and openness in his heart. And an example: if one of these great and mighty ones bought something from someone and paid him its price, the seller would not obtain any cause for pride in that, nor would he have any status and worth among people; whereas what is obtained from the ruler by way of bestowal of obligation and favor is more delightful, more desirable, and more wholesome in the opinion of all rational people. And this is the case even though the change of state and alteration of condition is subject to possibility, though distant, and falls within the sphere of conception, though difficult in habits and rare. So how can it be imagined that His blessings—even if small in themselves and few in themselves—are spoiled by the attachment of obligation from the Almighty, the Majestic, the All-Compelling, the All-Powerful, to Whom everything, even if its magnitude is great and its importance immense, is within His dominion and subject to His compulsion? He honors whom He honors by His beneficence and favor, and humiliates whom He humiliates by His dishonor and degradation. There is no end to His kingdom and sovereignty, and no change in the abasement of the servant and his acknowledgment [of dependence]; rather, change and decay enter into the sphere [...]
Source pages p. 1027

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Ka'bi's objection. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, begins by stating the heading: 'Refutation of al-Ka'bi who says: Blessings are diminished by obligation.' Then he reports al-Ka'bi's claim: giving compensation as reward is more beneficial for the boy than giving it initially as a voluntary favor, because the latter involves obligation (manna) which diminishes the blessing, whereas compensation does not. Al-Ka'bi concludes that what is obtained through compensation is more wholesome and delightful. 

The refutation starts with a strong retort: 'This is the speech of one who does not know Allah Most High.' The author argues that all blessings are from Allah, and His obligation (manna) upon us is the greatest. Far from diminishing joy, His obligation increases it. He cites the Quranic verse (49:17): 'But Allah confers obligation upon you that He has guided you to faith.' If obligation spoiled blessings, guidance itself would be spoiled. 

Then the author analyzes the cause of spoiling in the witnessed world (al-shahid): it occurs when the benefactor and recipient are equal in essence (al-jawhar) but differ in rank and state. The beneficiary feels subservient because the benefactor is of the same kind but superior in wealth or status. This causes the blessing to be spoiled. However, this does not apply to Allah, who is not equal to His creatures in essence. 

To illustrate, the author gives an example: if a great king specially favors a commoner, the commoner feels immense joy and pride, not spoiling. The blessing is even more delightful than a commercial transaction where the buyer pays a fair price. The more remote the favor seems, the greater the joy. Therefore, how could anyone imagine that Allah's blessings—however small—are spoiled by His obligation, when He is the Almighty, the All-Compelling, to Whom everything is subject? The passage ends by affirming that Allah's kingdom is eternal and the servant's abasement is perpetual, while change and decay belong to creation.

Key Terms
الشاهد (the witnessed world/the analogical realm)
الجوهر (essence)
المنة (obligation)
نعمة (blessing)
السلطان (ruler)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The same dynamic of obligation spoiling blessings applies to Allah as it does among humans.
Correction: The cause of spoiling among humans (equality in essence) does not apply to Allah, who is incomparably superior, and thus His obligation enhances joy.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nasafi, what is the cause of blessing being spoiled by obligation in the witnessed world?
A) The benefactor is stingy.
B) The benefactor and beneficiary are equal in essence but differ in rank.
C) The blessing is too small.
D) The beneficiary is ungrateful.

Key Takeaway
Human obligation spoils only among equals; with the incomparable Creator, obligation magnifies the blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you receive a blessing from Allah, do you feel grateful or weighed down by the sense of obligation? What does your reaction reveal about your view of Allah’s majesty?
?
Think of a specific blessing you often take for granted. How would receiving it as a personal gift from the King of kings change your response today?
?
If Allah’s obligation magnifies joy, why do you sometimes resent His commands? Confess that struggle to Him now and ask for a heart that delights in His favor.

The Bakriyya Denial of Children's Pain
Al-Nasafi reports and refutes the claim that children do not feel pain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes the extreme denial of sensory evidence by the Bakriyya sect.

Core Idea
Denying obvious pain to children shows how heresy leads to absurdity.

Al-Nasafi presents an example of theological confusion gone extreme: a sect that denies children feel pain. This passage shows how far some groups go to protect their doctrines, ignoring direct observation. Let's examine the claim and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation to familiarize yourself with the content.
Notice the tone: the author presents this as an absurdity.
2
Identify the absurdity in the claimed position
The claim is that children do not feel pain even if their limbs are cut. Think about why this contradicts direct observation.
This is the core of the refutation.
3
Note the attribution and context
Observe that al-Nasafi attributes this view to Bakr bin 'Abd Rabbih and also mentions it was narrated from the Najdat. This gives historical context.
These are identified as deviant sects.
4
Reflect on the refutation method
Al-Nasafi refutes by showing that the claim denies clear sensory evidence (mushahada). Consider why this is a powerful argument.
No separate proof is needed; the absurdity is self-evident.

ثم اضطرت الحيرة لهم في هذه المسألة طائفة منهم إلى إنكار المشاهدة والخروج إلى التجاهل، فزعم أن الأطفال لا يتألمون ولو أن أوصالهم قطعت وجعلت أعضاؤهم إربا إربا لما تألموا بذلك وهو قول بكر بن عبد ربه رئيس البكرية من أهل البدع وهو المعروف بابن أخت عبد الواحد بن زيد. وروى يحيى بن كامل البصري المعروف بالحجدري هذه المقابلة أيضا عن النجدات
Then confusion forced a group among them regarding this issue to deny observation and to resort to feigned ignorance. They claimed that children do not feel pain, even if their limbs were cut and their body parts made into pieces, they would not feel pain thereby. This is the saying of Bakr bin 'Abd Rabbih, the leader of the Bakriyya, one of the people of innovation, known as the son of the sister of 'Abd al-Wahid bin Zaid. And Yahya bin Kamil al-Basri, known as al-Hajdari, also narrated this claim from the Najdat.
Source pages p. 1031

Commentary
This passage reports an extreme position held by a sect called al-Bakriyya, who denied that children experience pain, even under severe torture. The author (al-Nasafi) cites this as an example of the confusion (hayra) that leads people to deny obvious sensory evidence to maintain their theological system. He then attributes this view to Bakr bin 'Abd Rabbih, the leader of the Bakriyya, and mentions that it was also narrated from the Najdat (a Kharijite subgroup). This is a refutation by showing the absurdity of the claim, as it contradicts direct observation.

البكرية
النجدات

Misconception & Correction

Correction: This passage shows that it is a desperate denial of sensory evidence, not a reasoned stance.

Sectarian Denial of Children's Pain
Nasafi reports and condemns the sectarian denial of observable pain in children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme position of the Bakriyya and Najdat sects in denying observable pain in children and why it is considered a denial of observation (إنكار المشاهدة).

Core Idea
Denying what is plainly observed is the most extreme form of intellectual stubbornness.

In this passage, Nasafi identifies an astonishing claim: that children do not feel pain, even when their limbs are cut off. This view was held by the Bakriyya and Najdat sects, and Nasafi condemns it as a denial of observation. Let's examine the text and understand why the author treats this as a serious doctrinal deviation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim

The claim is that children do not feel pain even under severe torture.

3
Understand the concept of 'denial of observation'
Reflect on why this view is categorized as 'إنكار المشاهدة'. What does it mean to deny something that is directly observed?
This concept is central to refuting the sectarian position.

Authentication of the Hadith on Qadariyya
Nasafi authenticates hadith via istifada and critic expertise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the concept of istifada (widespread transmission) to authenticate a hadith and why he considers it beyond rejection.

Core Idea
Istifada makes a hadith so strong that no sect can deny it.

Imam Nasafi tackles a key hadith about the Qadariyya sect, which some might dismiss. He argues that its transmission is so widespread and well-known among hadith critics that rejecting it is impossible. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Nasafi presents the authentication claim.
The passage ends mid-sentence but the meaning is clear.
2
Understand 'istifada'
Istifada is a level of transmission below tawatur but still very strong. Nasafi uses it to claim the hadith's soundness.
3
Identify the supporting evidence
Nasafi says the hadith is famous among specialized hadith critics who distinguish authentic from weak. This fame makes rejection impossible.
These critics used jarh wa ta'dil, history, and tabaqat.
4
Consider the implication
If such a hadith cannot be rejected, then the Qadariyya doctrine is condemned. This is a strong theological argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في القدرية: صح المروي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على طريق الاستفاضة القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة صحة لم يجد أحد من فرق الأمة سبيلاً إلى دفعه، لاشتهاره في النقلة الذين تجردوا لنقد الأحاديث والتمييز بين صحيحها وسقيمها وثابتها ومردودها، واشتهروا بصناعة الجرح والتعديل ومعرفة التواريخ والعلم بالطبقات والتفرقة بين الثقات من
Speech about the Qadariyya: The narration from the Prophet, peace be upon him, has been authenticated via widespread transmission (istifada): 'Al-Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah.' Its authenticity is such that none of the sects of the ummah could find a way to reject it, due to its fame among the transmitters who dedicated themselves to scrutinizing hadiths and distinguishing between their authentic and weak, established and rejected [ones], and they became famous for the science of jarh wa ta'dil, knowledge of histories, knowledge of classes (tabaqat), and differentiation between reliable [transmitters] from...
Source pages p. 1033

Commentary
This passage is a statement about the authentication of a well-known hadith that identifies the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination) as the Magians (fire-worshippers) of this Muslim community. Imam al-Nasafi uses the concept of 'istifada' (widespread transmission falling short of tawatur but still strong) to declare the hadith's soundness. He argues that its level of authentication is so high that no sect within the ummah can reject it. This is due to its fame among the hadith critics who specialized in scrutinizing narratives and distinguishing between authentic (sahih) and weak (saqim), established (thabit) and rejected (mardud). These scholars were renowned for their expertise in the science of jarh wa ta'dil (criticism and validation of narrators), knowledge of historical timelines, the classification of narrators by tabaqat (classes), and their ability to differentiate between trustworthy narrators (thiqat) and others. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the intended meaning is clear: the hadith is undeniable due to its strong transmission chain.

Key Terms
القدرية
مجوس هذه الأمة
الاستفاضة
الجرح والتعديل
الطبقات
ثقات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'istifada' is the same as tawatur or that a hadith not reaching tawatur can be easily rejected.
Correction: Istifada is a strong level of transmission that, while not conclusively certain like tawatur, still obligates acceptance due to its widespread nature and fame among critics.

Checkpoint
On what basis does al-Nasafi claim that the hadith 'Al-Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' cannot be rejected?
A) It is mentioned in the Qur'an.
B) It is transmitted via istifada and well-known among hadith critics.
C) It is unanimously accepted by all Muslims.
D) It was narrated by a single trustworthy companion.

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi uses the concept of istifada and the recognized expertise of hadith critics to establish the hadith's authenticity beyond dispute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the hadith about Qadariyya is so authentic that no sect can deny it, why do you still find yourself hesitant to accept its condemnation? What is the state of your heart that resists this truth? Will you submit to it today?
?
The hadith critics dedicated their lives to distinguishing truth from falsehood. What have you dedicated your life to, and how does that compare to their seriousness in preserving the deen? What one change can you make to prioritize truth?
?
The Prophet (saw) called Qadariyya 'Magians of this ummah'. Do you truly believe that any belief contrary to qadr is shirk-like, or do you downplay it because it is comfortable? What will you do about it starting now?

The Authentic Hadith and the Identification with Mu'tazila
Establishing the hadith's authenticity and initial identification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for identifying the Qadariyya with the Mu'tazila according to the prophetic hadith and the initial reaction of the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The hadith 'Qadariyya are Magians' is authentic and all sects applied it to the Mu'tazila.

This lesson begins by establishing the authority of the hadith that condemns the Qadariyya. Through widespread transmission, the hadith is undeniable, and all Muslim sects interpreted it as referring to the Mu'tazila. The Mu'tazila's extreme discomfort with this label is a key point.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on authenticity
Read the first part of the Arabic text where the author affirms the hadith's authenticity through istifāḍa and the acceptance of hadith critics.
Notice the emphasis on the chain and the critics.
2
Identify the universal application
Observe that 'all the sects of the ummah' turned this hadith to the Mu'tazila.
This shows consensus on interpretation.
3
Note the Mu'tazila's reaction
See how the Mu'tazila rejected the label so strongly that they preferred accusations of heresy.
This highlights the stigma of the term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في القدرية:
صح المروي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على طريق الاستفاضة القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة صحة لم يجد أحد من فرق الأمة سبيلاً إلى دفعه، لاشتهاره في النقلة الذين تجردوا لنقد الأحاديث والتمييز بين صحيحها وسقيمها وثابتها ومردودها، واشتهروا بصناعة الجرح والتعديل ومعرفة التواريخ والعلم بالطبقات والتفرقة بين الثقات من الرواة والضعفاء منهم وتلقيبهم إياه بالقبول والشهادة له بالصدق والثبوت عن الصادق المصدق، ثم إن جميع فرق الأمة صرفوه إلى المعتزلة، وتبرأت المعتزلة عن الاسم وأبوا قبوله على وجه كانت التسمية بالزندقة والإلحاد عليهم أهون وأيسر من هذه التسمية، ثم زعموا أن ذلك مصروف إلى من يقول القدر خيره وشره من الله بدلالة حديث آخر روى عنه عليه السلام وهو أنه قال: "القدرية خصماء الله" ووجه دلالته أن خصم الله من يضيف ما قبح من فعله إليه ويقول إن الله تعالى هو الذي أراده وأوجده، لا من ينزهه عن القبائح والشرور، قالوا: والاتفاق في المقالة يدل على ذلك فإن المجوس يقولون: نكاح الأمهات والأخوات ووطئهن بإرادة الله تعالى، وكذا أنتم تقولون هكذا، قالوا فأما نحن نقول: ليس شيء من ذلك بإرادة الله تعالى، وقالوا: نحن ننفي القدر فنقول: الله تعالى لا يقدر الشرور والمعاصي وخصومنا يثبتون ذلك والاسم المأخوذ عن معنى يضاف إلى مثبته دون نافيه.

[القدرية هم المعتزلة]
وأما أهل الحق فإنهم قالوا: إن القدرية هم المعتزلة فإنه عليه السلام قال: "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة" ووجه الكشف عن المراد بهذا اللفظ والمسمى بهذا الاسم هو النظر في المقالات ليظهر أن المخالف للمجوس أي فريق والموافق فيما هو من خاصية مذاهبهم من هو، ولا وجه لذلك غير هذا.
The discussion on the Qadariyya:
The report from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that 'the Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' is authentically established through widespread transmission (istifāḍa) with such authenticity that no one from the sects of the ummah has found a way to reject it, due to its fame among the transmitters who devoted themselves to criticizing hadiths and distinguishing between their sound and weak, established and rejected, and who were renowned for the craft of jarḥ and taʻdīl and knowledge of histories and the science of classes and the distinction between reliable and weak narrators, and their designation of it with acceptance and testimony of its truth and establishment from the truthful and believed one (al-Ṣādiq al-Muṣaddiq). Then all the sects of the ummah turned it towards the Muʻtazila, and the Muʻtazila disassociated themselves from the name and refused to accept it to the point that being called apostates and heretics was easier and lighter for them than this designation. Then they claimed that it refers to those who say that destiny (al-qadar), its good and evil, is from God, based on another hadith reported from him, peace be upon him, namely his saying: 'The Qadariyya are the opponents of Allah.' The indication of which is that the opponent of Allah is one who ascribes what is evil from His action to Him and says that Allah, exalted, is the one who willed it and originated it, not one who declares Him transcendent of ugly things and evils. They said: And the agreement in doctrine indicates that, for the Magians say that marriage to mothers and sisters and intercourse with them is by the will of Allah, and likewise you say such. They said: As for us, we say: None of that is by the will of Allah, and they said: We deny qadar and say: Allah, exalted, does not have power over evils and sins, and our opponents affirm that, and the name derived from a meaning is attached to its affirmer, not its denier.

[The Qadariyya are the Muʻtazila]
As for the people of truth (Ahl al-Ḥaqq), they said: Indeed, the Qadariyya are the Muʻtazila, because he, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah.' And the way to reveal the intended meaning of this term and the one named by this name is by examining the doctrines to show which group opposes the Magians and which agrees in what is specific to their sects. And there is no way for that other than this.
Source pages p. 1033

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument about the identity of the Qadariyya condemned in the prophetic hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah.' The author first establishes the hadith's authenticity, noting its widespread transmission and acceptance among hadith critics. He then observes that all Muslim sects interpreted it as referring to the Mu'tazila, who vehemently rejected the label, preferring accusations of heresy. The Mu'tazila counter-argue by citing another hadith, 'The Qadariyya are the opponents of Allah,' claiming that it applies to those who attribute evil to God. They illustrate this by asserting that the Magians (Zoroastrians) claim incestuous acts are by God's will, and they accuse the orthodox (Ahl al-Hadith) of saying the same. The Mu'tazila declare that they themselves deny that such acts are by God's will and assert that God has no power over evils—thus the name 'Qadariyya' (derived from qadar, meaning 'power' or 'decree') properly applies to those who affirm qadar (i.e., the orthodox), not to those who deny it. In response, the author presents the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the orthodox Sunni camp): they state unequivocally that the Qadariyya are indeed the Mu'tazila. The method for uncovering this is to examine the doctrines of each group and see which aligns with the distinctive tenets of the Magians. The implication is that the Mu'tazila, by denying that God creates evil, actually agree with the Magians' dualistic separation of the source of good and evil, while the orthodox affirm that all things, including evil, are created by God. Thus the hadith's condemnation applies to the Mu'tazila.

Key Terms
القدرية
المجوس
المعتزلة
الاستفاضة
الجرح والتعديل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith's authenticity is contested or that the identification is simply a Sunni polemic.
Correction: The author argues the hadith is so well-established that no sect can reject it, and all sects initially turned it to the Mu'tazila, giving it broad acceptance.

Checkpoint
Which group did all sects of the ummah turn the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' to?
A) The Magians
B) The Mu'tazila
C) The Ahl al-Haqq
D) The Zindīqs

Key Takeaway
The hadith condemning the Qadariyya is authentic and universally interpreted as referring to the Mu'tazila, who strongly rejected the label.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were faced with an authentic hadith that seemed to implicate a group you sympathize with, would you have the courage to accept it as the Mu'tazila refused to? What label or association do you most fear being attached to your faith, and why? Take time today to search your heart and ensure you are not more afraid of a label than of the truth itself.
?
The scholars who devoted their lives to jarḥ and taʻdīl accepted this hadith as true. Are there any aspects of your belief or practice that you hold onto not because they are proven from revelation, but because they are comfortable or popular? Will you commit today to re-examine your convictions solely on the basis of authentic sources, even if it means embracing an uncomfortable truth?
?
The Mu'tazila preferred being called apostates and heretics over being called Qadariyya. Is there a sin or shortcoming in your life that you would rather be accused of something worse than to admit and repent from? What step will you take today to confront that weakness honestly before Allah?

The Mu'tazila's Counterargument and Ahl al-Haqq's Rebuttal
Presentation of Mu'tazila's counterargument and Ahl al-Haqq's rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's counterargument using another hadith and analogy with Magians, and the Ahl al-Haqq's reaffirmation of the original identification.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila argued that Qadariyya are those who affirm God's decree of evil, but Ahl al-Haqq rejected this.

Having established the initial identification, we now examine the Mu'tazila's defense. They cite another hadith and compare themselves to the Magians, claiming that their opponents are the real Qadariyya. The Ahl al-Haqq respond by reaffirming the original identification through examination of doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's argument
Read the passage where the Mu'tazila use the hadith 'Qadariyya are the opponents of Allah' and their comparison with Magians.
Note their reinterpretation of the term 'Qadariyya'.
2
Understand the analogy
See how the Mu'tazila equate the orthodox (who affirm qadar) with the Magians who attribute incestuous acts to God's will.
This is a tu quoque argument.
3
Analyze the Ahl al-Haqq's response
Read the Ahl al-Haqq's statement that the Qadariyya are indeed the Mu'tazila and the method of examining doctrines.
They imply that the Mu'tazila, by denying God's creation of evil, align with the Magians' dualism.
4
Reflect on the method
Consider how the Ahl al-Haqq use the comparison of doctrines to determine who the hadith refers to.
This highlights the importance of ʿilm al-kalām in refuting heresies.

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
Identifying the Qadariyya: The Mu'tazila
The author argues that Qadariyya refers to Mu'tazila based on hadith and doctrinal comparison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ahl al-Haqq identify the Qadariyya as the Mu'tazila, based on the prophetic hadith and doctrinal comparison with the Magians.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya are not those who affirm qadar, but the Mu'tazila who share doctrines with Magians.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a key theological identification. The author argues that the term 'Qadariyya' in the hadith refers not to those who affirm divine decree, but specifically to the Mu'tazila. The argument hinges on comparing doctrines with the Magians (Zoroastrians). Let's read the source to see how this is established.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the structure: a claim, a hadith, a method, and a conclusion.
Pay attention to how the author uses the hadith as evidence.
2
Identify the main claim and proof
The author states that Ahl al-Haqq say the Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila. The proof is the hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.'
This hadith is key to the argument.
3
Understand the method of identification
The author says the way to uncover who is meant by 'Qadariyya' is to examine the doctrines of different groups and see which one agrees with the Magians in distinctive doctrines.
This is a comparative doctrinal analysis.
4
Recognize the conclusion
After examining the doctrines, one knows that the Mu'tazila are the specific group that shares distinctive doctrines with the Magians, thus they are the Qadariyya.
The conclusion logically follows from the method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أهل الحق فإنهم قالوا: إن القدرية هم المعتزلة فإنه عليه السلام قال: "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة" ووجه الكشف عن المراد بهذا اللفظ والمسمى بهذا الاسم هو النظر في المقالات ليظهر أن المخالف للمجوس أي فريق والموافق فيما هو من خاصية مذاهبهم من هو ، ولا وجه لذلك غير هذا. ثم من عرف المذاهب ووقف على ما لفرق الأمة من المقالات عرف أن المعتزلة هم المخصوصون من فرق الأمة بمشاركة المجوس فيما هو من خصائص مذاهبهم (1).
As for the People of Truth, they indeed said: The Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila, for the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' And the way of disclosing the intended meaning by this word and the one named by this name is to examine the doctrines so that it becomes clear which faction opposes the Magians and which agrees with what is distinctive to their doctrines, and there is no way to that other than this. Then whoever knows the doctrines and comes to know what the factions of the community hold, knows that the Mu'tazila are the ones specifically from the factions of the community who share with the Magians in what is distinctive to their doctrines (1).
Source pages p. 1034

Commentary
This passage is a definitional argument identifying the referent of the term 'Qadariyya' as used in the hadith. The author states that the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) assert that the Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila. The proof is the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' To understand who is meant by this word, one must examine the doctrines of the various groups to see which faction opposes the Magians (i.e., differs from them) and which agrees with them in the distinctive features of their doctrines. There is no other way to determine this. Then, the author concludes that anyone who knows the doctrines and knows the positions of the different factions of the community will recognize that the Mu'tazila are the specific group from the community that shares with the Magians in the distinctive aspects of their doctrines. Footnote (1) likely contains a citation or additional comment, but it is not part of the main argument. The passage thus establishes that the term Qadariyya, which the Mu'tazila reject, properly applies to them because of their doctrinal agreement with the Magians on certain points.

Key Terms

المعتزلة
المجوس
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume 'Qadariyya' refers to those who affirm divine decree (qadar).
Correction: The passage shows that Ahl al-Haqq identify 'Qadariyya' as the Mu'tazila, who deny qadar in a certain sense, based on their doctrinal agreement with Magians.

Checkpoint
According to the Ahl al-Haqq, who are the Qadariyya mentioned in the hadith?
A) Those who affirm that all good and evil are from Allah
B) The Mu'tazila
C) The Magians (Zoroastrians)
D) Those who deny divine decree entirely

Key Takeaway
The term 'Qadariyya' in the hadith refers specifically to the Mu'tazila, as shown by their doctrinal agreement with the Magians.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says that identifying the Qadariyya requires examining doctrines. Have you ever lazily accepted a label without checking it against the Prophet's warning? What specific belief about divine decree do you hold that you must now compare to the standards of Ahl al-Haqq?
?
If the Prophet compares a group to Magians, it is a grave warning. Are there any doctrines in your heart that subtly elevate human will above divine decree? How will you uproot them today?
?
You now know that the Qadariyya are not those who simply discuss qadar but those who share doctrines with Magians. Does this make you fear that you might be following a path of the Mu'tazila unknowingly? Commit to one action this week to learn more about the correct belief in qadar from the People of Truth.

Mu'tazila Worse Than Magians in Attributing Partners
Author compares Mu'tazila to Magians, arguing Mu'tazila are worse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that the Mu'tazila are worse than the Magians in their attribution of partners to God.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila commit a greater shirk than Magians by attributing countless partners to God.

In this passage, the author compares the Mu'tazila to the Zoroastrian Magians, arguing that despite their monotheistic claims, the Mu'tazila actually fall into a worse form of polytheism. By examining their doctrines on divine power and the attribution of good and evil, the author shows that the Mu'tazila go beyond the Magians in affirming partners for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the author's argument. Notice that he begins by stating that the Magians opposed all religions with falsehood, then draws parallels with the Mu'tazila.
Pay attention to the repeated structure: 'المجوس ... وكذا المعتزلة ...'.
2
Identify the three comparison points
The author lists three areas where the Mu'tazila imitate the Magians: (1) attributing creation to more than one source, (2) restricting God's power to good only, and (3) affirming partners for God. Identify each point in the text.
The third point is where the author says the Magians are better off because they only affirm one partner.
3
Analyze the conclusion
The author concludes that the Magians are 'more fortunate' because they only affirm one partner, while the Mu'tazila affirm countless partners. Reflect on why this makes the Mu'tazila worse.
Consider the implications for tawhid.
4
Connect to previous discussion
The author references 'the issue of the creation of acts' (مسألة خلق الأفعال). This connects to a broader theological debate about human agency and divine power. Understand that this passage builds on that earlier discussion.
This reference shows the continuity of the author's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجوس فيما خالفوا به جميع أهل الأديان من القول الباطل وأربوا عليهم فيه، ثم المجوس جعلت العالم بالله وبغيره ولا قدرة له على ما هو لغيره ولا قدرة لذلك الغير على ما هو له، وكذا المعتزلة جعلوا بالله وبغيره من الخالقين ولا قدرة له على ما هو لغيره ولا قدرة لغيره على ما هو له، وكذا المجوس تأبى دخول ما هو قبيح تحت قدرة الله تعالى وقصرت قدرته على المحاسن، وكذا المعتزلة ساعدوهم على هذا الأصل، وبنوا عليه جميع مذاهبهم، بل المجوس أسعد حالاً، لأنهم ما أثبتوا العالم إلا لله تعالى ولآخر، فاقتصروا على إثبات شريك واحد له، والمعتزلة أثبتوا له ما لا يحصون من الشركاء، وكذا أولئك أدخلوا جميع المحاسن تحت قدرته والمعتزلة أضافوا حسن المحاسن إلى غيره ولم يثبتوا الله تعالى على مثل تلك المحاسن قدرة على ما قررنا في مسألة خلق الأفعال، وإذا عرف هذا ظهر المراد بالاسم، والله الموفق.
The Magians, in what they opposed all the people of religions with false statement, and they exceeded them in it. Then the Magians made the world from God and from other, and He has no power over what is for other, nor does that other have power over what is for Him. Likewise the Mu'tazila made (the world) from God and from other creators, and He has no power over what is for other, nor does other have power over what is for Him. Likewise the Magians refuse the entry of what is ugly under the power of God the Exalted and restricted His power to good things, and likewise the Mu'tazila assisted them on this principle, and built upon it all their schools. Rather, the Magians are more fortunate, because they only attributed the world to God the Exalted and to another, so they restricted themselves to affirming one partner for Him, while the Mu'tazila affirmed for Him partners beyond count. Likewise those (Magians) included all good things under His power, while the Mu'tazila attributed the goodness of good things to other than Him and did not affirm for God the Exalted power over such good things, as we established in the issue of the creation of acts. And when this is known, the intended meaning of the name becomes clear, and God is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 1036

Commentary
This passage is an argument comparing the Mu'tazila unfavorably to the Magians (Zoroastrians). The author begins by stating that the Magians disagreed with all religions through false statements and even exceeded them. He then explains that the Magians attribute the world to both God and another being, with each having power only over what belongs to them, not the other's domain. The Mu'tazila similarly attribute creation to God and other creators, limiting each's power. Furthermore, the Magians exclude evil from God's power, restricting it to good, and the Mu'tazila assist them in this principle, building their entire doctrine upon it. However, the author argues that the Magians are better off because they only affirm one partner for God, whereas the Mu'tazila affirm countless partners. The Magians assign all good to God's power, but the Mu'tazila attribute goodness to other than God and deny God power over such good, referencing the earlier discussion on the creation of acts. The passage concludes that understanding this clarifies the meaning of the name (i.e., why they are called Mu'tazila) and ends with a prayer.

Key Terms
مجوس
معتزلة
قدرة
شركاء
محاسن
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila are better than the Magians because they are monotheists.
Correction: The passage argues that the Mu'tazila affirm countless partners for God, making them worse than the Magians who only affirm one partner. Thus, Mu'tazila are more blameworthy despite appearing monotheistic.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the Magians are 'more fortunate' (أسعد حالاً) than the Mu'tazila?
A) Because the Magians believe in one God while the Mu'tazila believe in many gods.
B) Because the Magians only affirm one partner for God, while the Mu'tazila affirm countless partners.
C) Because the Magians accept both good and evil from God, while the Mu'tazila reject evil.
D) Because the Magians are older and thus have more followers.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila, despite their monotheistic claims, are more blameworthy than the Magians because they attribute creation and goodness to countless partners of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something good, do you habitually thank God alone, or do you also subtly credit your own intelligence, effort, or the help of others? In light of this lesson, examine how many 'partners' you rely on in your heart every day.
?
The Mu'tazila attributed the goodness of good things to other than God. Is there an area in your life where you believe you are the source of goodness, shutting God out? Ask yourself: What would it take for you to truly attribute all goodness to God alone, even when you feel you contributed?
?
You might think that affirming one God is enough. But this lesson shows that even subtle associations—like limiting God's power only to good—are a form of shirk. Are you comfortable with God having power over every event in your life, including the difficult and ugly? If not, how can you begin to surrender that control to Him today?

Mu'tazila as the Real Opponents of God
Author contrasts Ahl al-Sunna submission with Mu'tazila disputation to prove the latter are God's opponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith on predestination and the contrasting attitudes of Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila prove that the Mu'tazila are the true opponents of God.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila dispute with God by imposing obligations on Him, while Ahl al-Sunna submit to His wisdom.

The author strengthens his previous argument by invoking a prophetic hadith that makes belief in predestination a condition of faith. He then contrasts two groups: those who accept God's decree without dispute, and those who challenge God with demands. This passage reveals the decisive difference that earns the Mu'tazila the title 'opponents of God'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the strong language used against the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify the hadith and its role
Find the hadith about predestination. Why does the author bring it here? It supports the claim that Mu'tazila side with the Magians against the Prophet.
The hadith makes qadar a condition of faith.
3
Analyze the description of Ahl al-Sunna
List the characteristics: they don't dispute punishment, don't demand reward, face calamities with patience, acknowledge God's ownership.
Their attitude is submission without demands.
4
Analyze the description of Mu'tazila
List their demands: God must do what is most beneficial, reward obedience, compensate for pain. They even say God would become unjust if He fails.
They place obligations on God as if He were a mere owner.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Read the final sentence. The author says anyone who thinks Ahl al-Sunna are the opponents is obstinate. Why does this follow from the contrast?
The contrast shows Mu'tazila are the ones disputing with God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيد هذا ما رواه غير واحد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم "القدر خيره وشره من الله تعالى". وروى أنه جعل هذا من شرط الإيمان والمجوس يكذبونه في ذلك وساعدت المعتزلة المجوس على تكذيب النبي عليه السلام في ذلك، وما روت المعتزلة من الحديث من أدل الدلائل على أن الاسم واقع عليهم دون خصمائهم فإن خصماءهم وإن قالوا إن الله تعالى هو الخالق لأفعالهم إلا أنهم لا يخاصمونه في التعذيب على ما قبح منها بل يرون ذلك حكمة وعدلاً، وكذا تخليقه على ما مر قبل هذا، وكذا لا يطالبونه بثواب ما أتوا به من الطاعات ويقولون ما أدينا إلا حقك المحن والمصائب قابلوا ذلك منه بالصبر وطلبوا منه إزالة ذلك بفضله وكرمه ولا يطالبون على ذلك منه عوضاً إقراراً منهم أن أنفسهم وأموالهم له يتصرف بذلك كله في ملكه يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد لا يسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون، فأما المعتزلة فهم الذين يخاصمونه ابتداء وانتهاء، فيقولون له ليس لك أن تفعل بنا إلا ما هو الأصلح لنا، وأن مصالحنا واجب عليك إعطاؤها وهي حق لنا مستحق قبلك إن لم تؤدها إلينا صرت ظالمًا جائراً ، سفيها مانعا حقا عليك ولا بقاء لك على ربوبيتك وسلطانك إلا بأداء ما هو حقنا قبلك، وإذا أطعناك بشيء مما أمرت وأدينا شكر بعض ما أوفيتنا من حقوقنا الواجبة عليك وجبت عليك مكافأتنا على ذلك ومقابلتنا بالإثابة على ما أدينا من حقك قبلنا لا يسعك إلا الخروج عن ذلك، وليس لك أن تؤلمنا من غير سابقة جناية إلا بشرط أن تعوضنا عن ذلك كما هو على كل من يتعرض ملك غيره ويتجاوز تصرفه عما هو مملوك له، ثم من عرف المذهبين وجعل الفريق الأول خصماء الله تعالى دون الفريق الثاني فهو مكابر معاند.
And this is supported by what more than one narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Predestination (al-qadar), its good and its evil, is from God the Exalted.' And it was narrated that he made this a condition of faith, and the Magians deny him in that, and the Mu'tazila helped the Magians in denying the Prophet (peace be upon him) in that. And what the Mu'tazila narrated from the hadith is among the strongest evidences that the name (opponent of God) applies to them rather than to their opponents. For their opponents, even though they say that God the Exalted is the Creator of their actions, yet they do not dispute with Him regarding punishment for what is ugly from them, but rather they consider that wisdom and justice. Likewise regarding His creation as passed before this. Likewise they do not demand from Him reward for the acts of obedience they performed, and they say: 'We have only fulfilled Your right upon us.' Calamities and afflictions they face from Him with patience and ask Him to remove that by His favor and generosity, and they do not demand compensation from Him for that, acknowledging that their selves and their wealth are His; He disposes of all that in His kingdom, doing what He wills and judging what He desires; He is not asked about what He does, while they are asked. As for the Mu'tazila, they are the ones who dispute with Him from beginning to end, saying to Him: 'You may not do to us except what is most beneficial for us, and our benefits are obligatory upon You to give, and they are a right due from You. If You do not deliver them to us, You become unjust, oppressive, foolish, preventing a right upon You, and there is no permanence for You in Your lordship and authority except by fulfilling what is our right from You. And if we obey You in something You commanded and fulfill gratitude for some of the rights You gave us that are obligatory upon You, then reward for that and recompense with reward for what we have fulfilled of Your right from us becomes obligatory upon You; You have no escape from that. And You may not cause us pain without previous injury except on condition that You compensate us for that, as is the case for anyone who interferes with another's property and exceeds his disposal beyond what is owned by him.' Then whoever knows the two schools and makes the first group the opponents of God the Exalted rather than the second group is an obstinate stubborn person.
Source pages p. 1036

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and classification. The author supports the earlier argument (that Mu'tazila are worse than Magians) with a hadith: 'Predestination, its good and its evil, is from God,' which the Magians deny, and the Mu'tazila help them in that denial. The author then argues that the very hadith which the Mu'tazila narrate against their opponents actually proves that the name 'opponent of God' applies to them, not to their opponents (Ahl al-Sunna). He contrasts the two groups: The opponents (Ahl al-Sunna) acknowledge that God creates their actions, but they do not dispute with Him about punishing what is ugly; they consider it wisdom and justice. They do not demand reward for obedience, saying they only fulfilled God's right. They face calamities with patience and ask for removal by God's favor, not demanding compensation, recognizing that all they have belongs to God. In contrast, the Mu'tazila dispute with God from start to finish. They claim God must do what is most beneficial for them, that benefits are obligatory upon God and are their due right; if God fails to give them, He becomes unjust and loses lordship. They demand reward for obedience as an obligation, and they require compensation for any pain without prior sin, as if God were a mere owner of property. The passage concludes that anyone who thinks the first group (Ahl al-Sunna) are God's opponents rather than the second is obstinate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila are the true defenders of God's justice.
Correction: They impose their own standards of justice on God, disputing His actions and demanding obligations, while Ahl al-Sunna submit to His wisdom without demanding anything.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main difference between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila in their attitude toward God's actions?
A) Ahl al-Sunna believe God is unjust while Mu'tazila believe He is just.
B) Ahl al-Sunna do not dispute God's actions and consider them wise, while Mu'tazila impose obligations on God and dispute with Him.
C) Ahl al-Sunna demand reward while Mu'tazila do not.
D) Ahl al-Sunna deny qadar while Mu'tazila affirm it.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's demand that God must act for their benefit and reward their obedience proves they are the ones who dispute with Him, not Ahl al-Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a hardship, do you catch yourself thinking that God 'owes' you relief or that your patience obligates Him to reward you? How does the Mu'tazila's attitude mirror your own in that moment?
?
The Mu'tazila say to God: 'You may not do to us except what is most beneficial for us.' Is there a specific area of your life—your health, your wealth, your relationships—where you are dictating to God what He must do? What would it mean to truly hand that area back to Him as His property?
?
You acknowledge that God is the Creator of your actions. But do you secretly feel that your good deeds earn you a right to Paradise? The passage says Ahl al-Sunna say: 'We have only fulfilled Your right upon us.' Can you say that from your heart? If not, what keeps you from that submission?

Refuting the Charge of Agreement with Magians
Author refutes claim of agreement between Ahl al-Sunna and Magians on marriage of daughters by will of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Magians' apparent agreement with Ahl al-Sunna on attributing events to God's will is not true agreement, because they differ on the underlying cause.

Core Idea
Agreement on words is not agreement on doctrine.

This passage is a sharp refutation of an accusation. Some claimed that Ahl al-Sunna support Magian practices by saying that even sinful acts are by God's will. The author clarifies that the Magians only say that because they think those acts are good, while Ahl al-Sunna affirm God's will over all events without exception. The difference in reasoning reveals a fundamental disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's tone: he calls the claim 'pure deception'.
The author uses strong language to dismiss the objection.
2
Identify the two reasoning patterns
Find how the Magians attribute acts to God's will (because they think the act is good) versus how Ahl al-Sunna do (because all events are by God's will). The commentary explains this difference.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that superficial agreement with different underlying causes is not true agreement. This is the key takeaway.
This refutes the accusation of complicity with Magians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زعموا من مساعدتنا المجوس بقولنا: إن نكاح البنات بإرادة الله تعالى تمويه محض، فإنهم يضيفون ذلك إلى الله تعالى بناء على ظنهم الكاذب أن ذلك مشروع وهو حسن ولو علموا قبحه لساعدوا المعتزلة في نفي إرادة الله تعالى عن ذلك، ألا ترى أنك لو سألتهم عن علة إضافتهم ذلك إلى إرادة الله تعالى اعتلوا بكونه حسنًا لا بكونه محدثًا ، فإذا هم مع المعتزلة في علة جواز الإضافة والمنع، وخالفونا أشد المخالفة كما خالفتنا المعتزلة، إلا أنهم ظنا منهم أن ذلك حسن ساعدونا في الظاهر والمساعدة في الظاهر مع الاختلاف في العلة لن يعد موافقة.
And what they claimed of our helping the Magians by our saying: 'Indeed, marriage of daughters is by the will of God the Exalted' is pure deception. For they (the Magians) attribute that to God the Exalted based on their false assumption that it is permissible and good. Had they known its ugliness, they would have helped the Mu'tazila in negating the will of God the Exalted from that. Do you not see that if you asked them about the reason for their attribution of that to the will of God the Exalted, they would give as reason its being good, not its being originated? Then they are with the Mu'tazila in the reason for permissibility of attribution and prohibition, and they opposed us most severely as the Mu'tazila opposed us, except that they, assuming that it is good, helped us in appearance. And help in appearance along with difference in cause is not considered agreement.
Source pages p. 1037

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The objectors claim that Ahl al-Sunna help the Magians by saying that marriage of daughters (implying possibly incestuous marriages practiced by Magians) is by God's will. The author calls this 'pure deception' (تمويه محض). He explains that the Magians attribute such acts to God because they falsely believe they are permissible and good. If they knew they were ugly, they would join the Mu'tazila in denying God's will from them. The proof: if you ask them why they attribute it to God's will, they cite its goodness, not its origination (as a created act). In this reasoning (considering goodness the criterion), they agree with the Mu'tazila on the principle of what can be attributed to God, differing from Ahl al-Sunna who attribute all acts to God's will regardless of moral status. Thus, the Magians' apparent agreement with Ahl al-Sunna in wording (attributing to God's will) is only superficial; they fundamentally disagree on the cause. Such superficial agreement with difference in underlying principle is not true agreement.

Key Terms
نكاح البنات
إرادة الله
موافقة
علة
حسن
قبح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ahl al-Sunna and Magians agree on attributing evil acts to God's will.
Correction: Magians only attribute such acts to God's will because they believe the acts are good. Ahl al-Sunna attribute all events to God's will regardless of moral status. The difference in reasoning means the agreement is only apparent.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the Magians' attribution of marriage of daughters to God's will is not true agreement with Ahl al-Sunna?
A) Because the Magians deny God's will in other matters.
B) Because the Magians attribute it based on its goodness, not because it occurs, while Ahl al-Sunna attribute all events to God's will.
C) Because the Magians only pretend to agree but actually disagree.
D) Because the Magians do not believe in God at all.

Key Takeaway
Superficial agreement in wording does not imply doctrinal unity when the underlying reasoning differs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever defended a belief or action simply because it sounded similar to what others say, without examining the deeper reason behind it? Will you now commit to understanding the 'cause' (ʿilla) behind your convictions, even if it is uncomfortable?
?
The Magians justified wrong acts by calling them good. Are there habits in your life that you have convinced yourself are acceptable, when deep down you know they conflict with God's law? What step will you take today to stop rationalizing and start repenting?
?
This lesson shows that agreement in words can hide deep disagreement in truth. Are you more concerned with appearing to agree with others to avoid conflict than with standing firmly on sound doctrine? Will you courageously clarify the real reasons for your beliefs, even if it means being misunderstood?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
Outward Agreement vs. Real Agreement
Refutes the claim that Maturidis agree with Magians on marriage of daughters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why outward similarity in attributing acts to God does not imply real agreement if the basis of attribution is fundamentally different.

Core Idea
Outward agreement does not equal theological agreement when the reasons differ.

This passage addresses a common polemical accusation: that the Maturidi view on God's will agrees with the Magian view. The author shows that this is a misunderstanding — the two sides attribute acts to God for entirely different reasons. We will examine how he distinguishes real agreement from mere outward similarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the author's tone and structure.
Pay attention to the key term 'علة' (cause/reason).
2
Identify the Magians' reason
The author explains why the Magians attribute marriage of daughters to God's will. Find that reason and note it.
They consider the act good (حسن), not originated (محدث).
3
Contrast with the Maturidi reason
From the author's argument, infer what the Maturidi reason would be. The passage implies it is based on origination (huduth), not goodness.
If they knew it was evil, they would side with the Mu'tazila in negating God's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفنا بمساعدة المجوس تمويه محض وما زعموا من مساعدتنا المجوس بقولنا: إن نكاح البنات بإرادة الله تعالى تمويه محض، فإنهم يضيفون ذلك إلى الله تعالى بناء على ظنهم الكاذب أن ذلك مشروع وهو حسن ولو علموا قبحه لساعدوا المعتزلة في نفي إرادة الله تعالى عن ذلك، ألا ترى أنك لو سألتهم عن علة إضافتهم ذلك إلى إرادة الله تعالى اعتلوا بكونه حسنًا لا بكونه محدثًا، فإذا هم مع المعتزلة في علة جواز الإضافة والمنع، وخالفونا أشد المخالفة كما خالفتنا المعتزلة، إلا أنهم ظنا منهم أن ذلك حسن ساعدونا في الظاهر والمساعدة في الظاهر مع الاختلاف في العلة لن يعد موافقة. والله الموفق.
And their claim that we help the Magians is pure deception, and what they alleged about our helping the Magians by our statement: 'Marriage of daughters is by the will of God' is pure deception. For they (the Magians) attribute that to God based on their false assumption that it is permissible and good. If they knew its evil, they would help the Mu'tazila in negating the will of God from that. Do you not see that if you asked them about the reason for their attribution of that to the will of God, they would adduce that it is good, not that it is originated? Thus they are with the Mu'tazila regarding the reason for the permissibility of attribution and prohibition, and they oppose us severely just as the Mu'tazila opposed us. However, because they thought it is good, they helped us outwardly, and outward help with difference in the reason does not count as agreement. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1037

Commentary
This passage refutes the accusation that the Maturidis agree with the Magians (Zoroastrians) regarding the attribution of marriage of daughters to God's will. The author explains that the Magians attribute it to God because they mistakenly think it is good and permissible. If they realized it is evil, they would join the Mu'tazila in denying God's will from such acts. The key difference is the reason: the Magians base attribution on goodness (husn), while the Maturidis base it on origination (huduth) or divine omnipotence. Thus, even though there is an outward similarity in attributing the act to God, the underlying principles are opposite, so it is not real agreement.

Correction: The author shows that the agreement is only outward; the underlying reasons are opposites: Magians base attribution on goodness, Maturidis on origination.

Checkpoint

C) Because the Magians are Zoroastrians.
D) Because the author's school denies that marriage of daughters is by God's will.

Key Takeaway
Outward similarity in attributing actions to God does not constitute real agreement if the underlying principle (ʿilla) is different.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What specific action will you re-align today so that your motive is purely obedience to Him, not your own approval?
?
When you meet someone who shares your words but not your theological foundation—perhaps a nominal Muslim who prays but denies God's attributes—do you assume we are united, or do you discern the difference? What step will you take to verify the basis of agreement before building alliance?
?
The Magians could not see the evil in their practices and so they mistakenly attributed them to God. Are you currently justifying a wrong habit by thinking 'it must be God's will' instead of judging it by the Qur'an and Sunna? What is one habit you have rationalized, and what concrete step will you take to bring it in line with revelation?

Who Deserves the Name Qadariyya?
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila claim to the name Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila's claim to the name Qadariyya by exposing their deception in affirming power for themselves while denying it for God.

Core Idea
The name Qadariyya belongs to those who affirm power for themselves, not for God.

In this passage, al-Nasafi responds to the Mu'tazila's attempt to claim the name Qadariyya for themselves. He argues that their outward agreement with the Ahl al-Sunna is deceptive, as the underlying cause differs. He then exposes their inconsistency: they affirm power for themselves but deny it for God, making them more deserving of the name.

Guided Path
1
Context of the dispute
Understand that the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna dispute over the name Qadariyya. The Mu'tazila claim the name because they affirm human power (qadariyya) as a principle.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: first a remark about outward aid, then the main argument about power attribution.
3
Analyze the first point
Identify al-Nasafi's claim that outward agreement is not true agreement when the cause differs. This undermines the Mu'tazila's pretense of harmony.
The phrase 'موافقة' (agreement) is key.
4
Examine the deception (tamwih)
Focus on al-Nasafi's argument: the Mu'tazila claim to affirm power while the Ahl al-Sunna deny it. But the Ahl al-Sunna affirm power for God, while the Mu'tazila affirm it for themselves. Therefore, the name Qadariyya (those who affirm power) applies more to the Mu'tazila.
The reasoning turns on who the power is attributed to.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why al-Nasafi ends with 'Wa Allah al-Muwaffiq.' The argument is presented as sound reasoning, but ultimate success is from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخالفونا أشد المخالفة كما خالفتنا المعتزلة، إلا أنهم ظنا منهم أن ذلك حسن ساعدونا في الظاهر والمساعدة في الظاهر مع الاختلاف في العلة لن يعد موافقة. والله الموفق. وما قالوا أنا ننفي القدرة وأنتم تثبتون القدرة فكانت إضافة الاسم إلى المثبت أولى من إضافته إلى النافى تمويه آخر، وذلك أنا أثبتنا لغيرنا وهو الله تعالى وهم أثبتوا ذلك لأنفسهم، وعند التعارض كان إثبات الاسم لمن أثبت ذلك لنفسه أولى من إثباته لمن ينفيه عن نفسه ويثبت ذلك لغيره، والله الموفق.
And they opposed us most severely as the Mu'tazila opposed us, except that they thought in their opinion that that is good, they aided us outwardly, and outward aid with difference in the cause is not counted as agreement. And God is the granter of success. And what they said: 'We negate power and you affirm power,' so the attribution of the name to the affirmer is more appropriate than its attribution to the denier is another deception. And that is that we affirmed it for other than us, namely God Almighty, and they affirmed it for themselves, and when there is conflict, the attribution of the name to the one who affirmed it for himself is more appropriate than its attribution to the one who denies it for himself and affirms it for another. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 1038

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised by the Mu'tazila regarding the name 'Qadariyya'. The author begins by noting that the Mu'tazila outwardly agreed with them on some points but disagrees in the underlying cause, which does not constitute true agreement. He then addresses the Mu'tazila's claim that they (the Ahl al-Sunna) deny power (al-qudra) while the Mu'tazila affirm it. Al-Nasafi argues that the attribution of the name 'Qadariyya' should go to those who affirm power for themselves, not to those who affirm it for God. Since the Mu'tazila affirm power for themselves and deny it for God, they deserve the name. The Ahl al-Sunna, by contrast, affirm power for God alone and deny it for themselves. Therefore, it is more appropriate to apply the name to the Mu'tazila. The passage ends with 'And God is the granter of success.'

Key Terms
قدرة (power)
إضافة الاسم (attribution of the name)
موافقة (agreement)
تمويه (deception)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the name Qadariyya applies to those who deny qadar (divine decree) or those who affirm human free will absolutely.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues the name Qadariyya applies to those who affirm power (qudra) for themselves, not for God. The Mu'tazila affirm power for themselves, so they deserve the name, while the Ahl al-Sunna affirm power for God and deny it for themselves.

Checkpoint

B) Because they affirm power for themselves and deny it for God.
C) Because they outwardly agreed with the Ahl al-Sunna.
D) Because they claimed to be the true Qadariyya.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila's claim to the name Qadariyya by showing that they affirm power for themselves, making them the true Qadariyya, while the Ahl al-Sunna affirm power only for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Mu'tazilite Argument on the Name 'Fasiq' for the Grave Sinner
Mu'tazilites argue that the grave sinner should be called fasiq, not mu'min or kafir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that the grave sinner should be called fasiq exclusively, based on the consensus of the early community and the dichotomy between good and evil names.

Core Idea
Consensus on a name is not enough; the Mu'tazila use it to deny the grave sinner the title mu'min.

In this passage, the Mu'tazilites present their reasoning for calling the grave sinner a fasiq. They review the three opinions of the early community, note the agreed-upon name, and then adopt it exclusively. This argument is central to the Mu'tazilite position on the intermediate status between faith and disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying three opinions
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Identify the three groups mentioned and their respective positions on the grave sinner.
Notice that each group combines a different label (mu'min, kāfir, munāfiq) with fasiq.
2
Examine the Mu'tazilite use of consensus
Observe that the Mu'tazila argue from the agreement of all groups on the name fasiq. They claim that because the umma agreed on fasiq, that name should be used exclusively.
Think about the logical move from 'everyone agrees on this name' to 'this is the only correct name'.
3
Understand the reasoning from good and evil names
The passage concludes that since the grave sinner is called by evil names (fasiq, unjust, etc.), he should not be called by the good name mu'min. Reflect on how this connects to the Mu'tazilite view of the grave sinner's status.
This reasoning assumes a stark dichotomy between good and evil names.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعتزلة يزعمون في الاسم أن الناس اختلفوا في صاحب الكبيرة على أقوال منهم من قال : إنه مؤمن بما معه من التصديق فاسق بما اقترف من الذنب وهو قول الجماعة، ومنهم من قال : إنه كافر وهو فاسق وهو قول الخوارج، ومنهم من قال هو منافق فاسق وهو قول الحسن ومن تابعه، فاتفقت الأمة على إطلاق اسم الفاسق واختلفوا في إطلاق اسم المؤمن والكافر والمنافق، فأخذنا نحن بما اتفقوا عليه وهو اسم الفاسق وتركنا ما اختلفوا فيه قلنا: إنه فاسق وليس بمؤمن ولا كافر ولا منافق ولأنه لما سمي بالأسماء الخبيثة كالفاسق والجائر والفاجر والظالم لا يسمى بالأسماء الطيبة، والمؤمن من الأسماء الطيبة
The Mu'tazilites claim regarding the name that the people differed over the grave sinner according to several opinions: among them are those who said: He is a believer (mu'min) due to the affirmation (tasdiq) he possesses, and a sinner (fasiq) due to the sin he committed – and that is the opinion of the generality (jamāʿa). Among them are those who said: He is a disbeliever (kāfir) and a sinner (fāsiq) – and that is the opinion of the Khawārij. Among them are those who said: He is a hypocrite (munāfiq) and a sinner (fāsiq) – and that is the opinion of al-Ḥasan and those who followed him. The umma agreed upon applying the name fasiq, and differed over applying the names mu'min, kāfir, and munāfiq. So we took what they agreed upon, which is the name fasiq, and left what they differed over. We said: He is a fasiq, not a mu'min, nor a kāfir, nor a munāfiq. And because since he is called by evil names, like fasiq, jā'ir, fājir, ẓālim, he is not called by good names, and mu'min is among the good names.
Source pages p. 1046

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite argument for calling the grave sinner (ṣāḥib al-kabīra) a fasiq. It begins by noting that the umma (the early community) had three views on the grave sinner: some (the Jamāʿa) said he is a mu'min due to his faith but a fasiq due to his sin; the Khawārij said he is a kāfir and a fasiq; al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī and his followers said he is a munāfiq and a fasiq. The Mu'tazila then observe that all three groups agreed on calling him fasiq, but disagreed on the other names. Seizing on this consensus, the Mu'tazila adopt the name fasiq exclusively and reject the other names. Their reasoning is that a person who is called by evil names (like fasiq, unjust, wicked, oppressor) should not be called by a good name like mu'min. Thus, the grave sinner is merely a fasiq, not a believer.

Key Terms
فاسق
مؤمن
كافر
منافق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila deny that the grave sinner has any faith.
Correction: The Mu'tazila affirm that the grave sinner has tasdiq (affirmation) but deny him the name mu'min, calling him fasiq instead.

Checkpoint
What name do the Mu'tazila give to the grave sinner?
A) Mu'min
B) Kafir
C) Fasiq
D) Munafiq

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argue that the grave sinner is exclusively a fasiq, based on the consensus of the umma on that name and the principle that evil names preclude good names.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you immediately strip them of the title 'believer' in your heart? How does the Mu'tazilite argument, which uses consensus to deny the name mu'min, expose a similar tendency in you to judge based on partial evidence? Will you repent and strive to see the remaining faith in a sinner?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that evil names preclude good ones. In your own life, do you reduce people to their worst action, labeling them as 'sinner' or 'hypocrite' while ignoring their good deeds and faith? How can you break this habit and treat others with the complexity they deserve?
?
If the umma agreed on one label (fasiq) but differed on others, the Mu'tazila took only the agreed label. Are you quick to adopt harsh labels for others because they are popular or agreed upon, rather than holding onto the more balanced view of the Jama'a (believer despite sin)? Will you commit today to defend the faith of a struggling Muslim, even when their sins are evident?

Refutation of Mu'tazila Claim of Consensus on Fisq
The author refutes the Mu'tazila argument that calling a major sinner 'fasiq' is consensual while other terms are disputed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila argument about consensus on the term 'fasiq' is flawed and how the author refutes it.

Core Idea
Consensus on a term does not prove its correctness when the consensus itself is disputed.

The Mu'tazila argued that since everyone agrees that a major sinner is 'fasiq,' that term should be used, while other terms are disputed. But is that consensus genuine? In this passage, the author exposes the flaw in their reasoning, showing that the claimed consensus is not established.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila argument
Read the first part of the passage where the Mu'tazila present their claim: that applying 'fasiq' is agreed upon, while terms like 'believer' are disputed, so they adopt the agreed term.
Notice that they present this as a methodological principle.
2
See the author's refutation
Read the author's response: he declares their claim false because they are taking the agreed-upon while ignoring that there is opposition to that very consensus.
The key is that their consensus is not real—it's disputed.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this refutation matters: consensus arguments must be established before they can be used. Just claiming consensus does not make it true.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلان قول المعتزلة بالإجماع على الفسق[ ثم ما تزعم المعتزلة أن إطلاق اسم الفسق مجمع عليه وإطلاق ما وراء ذلك من اسم المؤمن والكافر والمنافق مختلف فيه فأخذنا بالمجمع عليه وتركنا المختلف فيه. كلام باطل، إذ هو أخذ بالمجمع عليه وأعرض عن المخالفة
Refutation of the Mu'tazila claim of consensus on fisq: Then what the Mu'tazila claim—that applying the term 'fasiq' is agreed upon (mujma' 'alayh) and applying other terms like 'believer,' 'disbeliever,' and 'hypocrite' are subject to disagreement—so we adopt what is agreed upon and leave what is disagreed upon. This statement is false, for it is adopting the agreed-upon while turning away from opposition [to it].
Source pages p. 1048

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific argument by the Mu'tazila. They argued that the term 'fasiq' for a major sinner is a matter of consensus, while calling him 'believer' is disputed. Thus, they claimed it is safer to call him fasiq. The author responds that this is false because by taking the agreed-upon term 'fasiq' they are ignoring the fact that there is opposition [i.e., the Sunni position that he is still a believer] to that very claim of consensus. In other words, the consensus itself is disputed, not a given.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that if most people agree on a term, it must be the correct one to use, even if there is significant opposition.
Correction: The author shows that the claim of consensus itself can be disputed; one cannot simply adopt the 'agreed-upon' term when the consensus is not established.

Key Takeaway
A consensus argument is only as strong as the consensus itself; if the consensus is disputed, the argument collapses.

?
